id="cite_ref-LLUSA_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-LLUSA-5">[5]</a></sup><br/>\n<a href="/wiki/Raleigh,_North_Carolina" title="Raleigh, North Carolina">Raleigh, North Carolina</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wwebio_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-wwebio-6">[6]</a></sup><br/>\nSmithfield, North Carolina</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Debut</th>\n<td>1991<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hurricane_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-hurricane-7">[7]</a></sup></td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p><b>Gregory Shane Helms</b> (born July 12, 1974) is an American <a href="/wiki/Professional_wrestling" title="Professional wrestling">professional wrestler</a>. He is best known for his time with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Wrestling_Entertainment" title="World Wrestling Entertainment">World Wrestling Entertainment</a> (WWE), where he wrestled as <b>The Hurricane</b>, <b>Gregory Helms</b>, and <b>Hurricane Helms</b> and also for his time with <a href="/wiki/World_Championship_Wrestling" title="World Championship Wrestling">World Championship Wrestling</a> (WCW), where he wrestled as "<b>Sugar</b>" <b>Shane Helms</b>.</p>\n<p>Helms first began wrestling in 1991 at the age of 16, and wrestled in numerous <a href="/wiki/Independent_circuit" title="Independent circuit">independent</a> <a href="/wiki/Professional_wrestling_promotion" title="Professional wrestling promotion">promotions</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/OMEGA_Championship_Wrestling" title="OMEGA Championship Wrestling">Organization of Modern Extreme Grappling Arts</a>, winning numerous <a href="/wiki/Cruiserweight_(professional_wrestling)" title="Cruiserweight (professional wrestling)">light heavyweight</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tag_team" title="Tag team">tag team</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Championship_(professional_wrestling)" title="Championship (professional wrestling)">championships</a>. In 1999, he signed with WCW, and gained fame as "Sugar" Shane Helms, a member of <a href="/wiki/3_Count" title="3 Count">3 Count</a>. During his time there he won both the <a href="/wiki/WCW_Hardcore_Championship" title="WCW Hardcore Championship">WCW Hardcore Championship</a> and the <a href="/wiki/WWE_Cruiserweight_Championship_(1991%E2%80%932007)" title="WWE Cruiserweight Championship (1991\xe2\x80\x932007)">WCW Cruiserweight Championship</a>. When WCW was bought by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Wrestling_Entertainment" title="World Wrestling Entertainment">World Wrestling Federation</a> (WWF, now WWE), Helms\' contract was kept by WWF. Helms renamed himself "The Hurricane" and won the <a href="/wiki/WWE_Cruiserweight_Championship_(1991%E2%80%932007)" title="WWE Cruiserweight Championship (1991\xe2\x80\x932007)">WWE Cruiserweight Championship</a>. He later picked up a sidekick, <a href="/wiki/Rosey_(wrestler)" title="Rosey (wrestler)">Rosey</a>, and they won the <a href="/wiki/World_Tag_Team_Championship_(WWE)" title="World Tag Team Championship (WWE)">World Tag Team Championship</a> together.</p>\n<p>He dropped the superhero <a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_professional_wrestling_terms#Gimmick" title="Glossary of professional wrestling terms">gimmick</a> in 2005, and began wrestling under his real name. He once again won the Cruiserweight Championship in early 2006, and held it for over a year, becoming the longest reigning Cruiserweight Champion and the longest reigning champion of any kind in <a href="/wiki/WWE_SmackDown" title="WWE SmackDown">SmackDown</a> history. After being out of action for over a year after neck fusion surgery Helms returned to SmackDown in September 2008, referring to himself as Hurricane Helms, before moving to the <a href="/wiki/ECW_(WWE)" title="ECW (WWE)">ECW</a> brand where he reverted to his Gregory Helms name, and became the backstage interviewer. In mid-2009, he brought back The Hurricane character, and appeared as both Gregory Helms and The Hurricane on the ECW brand. After the ECW brand ended, Helms was released by WWE on February 26, 2010, and returned to the independent circuit.</p>\n<p></p>\n<div class="toc" id="toc">\n<div class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<p></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Professional_wrestling_career">Professional wrestling career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gregory_Helms&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Professional wrestling career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span id="Early_career_(1991\xe2\x80\x931999)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_career_.281991.E2.80.931999.29">Early career (1991\xe2\x80\x931999)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gregory_Helms&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early career (1991\xe2\x80\x931999)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Helms began wrestling at the age of 17 in 1991.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-slam_3-4"><a href="#cite_note-slam-3">[3]</a></sup> He won his first championship shortly afterwards, by defeating "Playboy" T.C. Cruise to become the Southern Wrestling Alliance (SWA) Light Heavyweight Champion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-slam_3-5"><a href="#cite_note-slam-3">[3]</a></sup> Helms spent the majority of his early career in his home state of <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">North Carolina</a>, winning numerous <a href="/wiki/Cruiserweight_(professional_wrestling)" title="Cruiserweight (professional wrestling)">light heavyweight</a> championships.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-slam_3-6"><a href="#cite_note-slam-3">[3]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Helms began calling himself "The Show" Shane Helms, and <a href="/wiki/Tag_team" title="Tag team">teamed</a> with "Big Daddy" Mike Maverick, initially using the team name Assault and Battery.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-slam_3-7"><a href="#cite_note-slam-3">[3]</a></sup> They later dubbed themselves The Serial Thrillaz, and won several <a href="/wiki/Independent_circuit" title="Independent circuit">independent</a> tag championships.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-slam_3-8"><a href="#cite_note-slam-3">[3]</a></sup> The pair also began wrestling in the <a href="/wiki/OMEGA_Championship_Wrestling" title="OMEGA Championship Wrestling">Organization of Modern Extreme Grappling Arts</a> (OMEGA), which was founded by <a href="/wiki/The_Hardy_Boyz" title="The Hardy Boyz">The Hardy Boyz</a> (<a href="/wiki/Matt_Hardy" title="Matt Hardy">Matt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Hardy" title="Jeff Hardy">Jeff</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-slam_3-9"><a href="#cite_note-slam-3">[3]</a></sup> The Serial Thrillaz won the <a href="/wiki/OMEGA_Tag_Team_Championship" title="OMEGA Tag Team Championship">OMEGA Tag Team Championship</a> twice between 1997 and 1998, before they began competing for <a href="/wiki/Southern_Championship_Wrestling" title="Southern Championship Wrestling">Southern Championship Wrestling</a> (SCW). They won the <a href="/wiki/SCW_Tag_Team_Championship" title="SCW Tag Team Championship">SCW Tag Team Championship</a>, and Helms also won the <a href="/wiki/SCW_Heavyweight_Championship" title="SCW Heavyweight Championship">SCW Heavyweight Championship</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-slam_3-10"><a href="#cite_note-slam-3">[3]</a></sup> SCW would mark the end of the Serial Thrillaz, as Helms vacated both titles before moving on to NWA Worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-slam_3-11"><a href="#cite_note-slam-3">[3]</a></sup> Once there, Helms joined the Bad Street Boys with <a href="/wiki/Shannon_Moore" title="Shannon Moore">Shannon Moore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christian_York" title="Christian York">Christian York</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adam_Birch" title="Adam Birch">Joey Matthews</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-slam_3-12"><a href="#cite_note-slam-3">[3]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span id="World_Championship_Wrestling_(1999\xe2\x80\x932001)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="World_Championship_Wrestling_.281999.E2.80.932001.29">World Championship Wrestling (1999\xe2\x80\x932001)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gregory_Helms&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: World Championship Wrestling (1999\xe2\x80\x932001)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/3_Count" title="3 Count">3 Count</a></div>\n<p>Helms and his friend <a href="/wiki/Shannon_Moore" title="Shannon Moore">Shannon Moore</a> signed with <a href="/wiki/World_Championship_Wrestling" title="World Championship Wrestling">World Championship Wrestling</a> (WCW) in May 1999.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-slam_3-13"><a href="#cite_note-slam-3">[3]</a></sup> In WCW, Helms, along with Moore and <a href="/wiki/Evan_Karagias" title="Evan Karagias">Evan Karagias</a>, formed the <a href="/wiki/Heel_(professional_wrestling)" title="Heel (professional wrestling)">heel</a> (villainous) <a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_professional_wrestling_terms#Stable" title="Glossary of professional wrestling terms">stable</a> (faction) <a href="/wiki/3_Count" title="3 Count">3 Count</a>, and the trio debuted on the December 23 episode of <i><a href="/wiki/WCW_Thunder" title="WCW Thunder">WCW Thunder</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wcwbio_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-wcwbio-8">[8]</a></sup> The trio was a <a href="/wiki/Parody" title="Parody">parody</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Boy_band" title="Boy band">boy bands</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%27N_Sync" title="\'N Sync">\'N Sync</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Backstreet_Boys" title="Backstreet Boys">Backstreet Boys</a>, and their <a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_professional_wrestling_terms#Gimmick" title="Glossary of professional wrestling terms">gimmick</a> involved making <a href="/wiki/Music_video" title="Music video">music videos</a> and performing songs before their matches.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hurricane_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-hurricane-7">[7]</a></sup></p>\n<p>3 Count collectively won the <a href="/wiki/WCW_Hardcore_Championship" title="WCW Hardcore Championship">WCW Hardcore Championship</a> on <i><a href="/wiki/WCW_Monday_Nitro" title="WCW Monday Nitro">WCW Monday Nitro</a></i> in February 2000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-slam_3-14"><a href="#cite_note-slam-3">[3]</a></sup> This win made 3 Count the first trio to win the Hardcore Championship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wcwbio_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-wcwbio-8">[8]</a></sup> At <a href="/wiki/WCW_Uncensored#2000" title="WCW Uncensored">Uncensored</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brian_Knobbs" title="Brian Knobbs">Brian Knobbs</a> defeated all members of 3 Count to win the Hardcore Championship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> During a match, Helms suffered a broken nose, and was sidelined while he recovered.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-slam_3-15"><a href="#cite_note-slam-3">[3]</a></sup> Upon his return, <a href="/wiki/Tank_Abbott" title="Tank Abbott">Tank Abbott</a> had been added to the group, as a fan, and was utilized in an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Enforcer_(professional_wrestling)" title="Enforcer (professional wrestling)">enforcer</a> role. 3 Count had a long-running <a href="/wiki/Feud_(professional_wrestling)" title="Feud (professional wrestling)">feud</a> (scripted rivalry) with <a href="/wiki/The_Jung_Dragons" title="The Jung Dragons">The Jung Dragons</a>, with the Dragons attempting to steal 3 Count\'s <a href="/wiki/Kayfabe" title="Kayfabe">fictional</a> recording contract.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-slam_3-16"><a href="#cite_note-slam-3">[3]</a></sup> This led to a <a href="/wiki/Ladder_match" title="Ladder match">ladder match</a> between the two teams at <a href="/wiki/New_Blood_Rising" title="New Blood Rising">New Blood Rising</a>, which 3 Count won due to Abbott\'s interference.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> As a result, Abbott claimed that he should be the lead singer of 3 Count, and was kicked out by the other three members, leading to a feud.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3_Count_OWOW_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-3_Count_OWOW-11">[11]</a></sup></p>\n<p>3 Count later disbanded as Moore and Helms kicked Karagias out of the group for attempting to steal the spotlight.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-slam_3-17"><a href="#cite_note-slam-3">[3]</a></sup> At the same time, the Jung Dragons turned on <a href="/wiki/Jamie_Noble" title="Jamie Noble">Jamie Noble</a>, who formed a team with Karagias.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-slam_3-18"><a href="#cite_note-slam-3">[3]</a></sup> The three teams met in a <a href="/wiki/Professional_wrestling_match_types#Basic_non-elimination_matches" title="Professional wrestling match types">Triangle match</a> at <a href="/wiki/WCW_Mayhem#2000" title="WCW Mayhem">Mayhem</a>, which 3 Count won.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> They also wrestled each other in a number one contendership ladder match at <a href="/wiki/Starrcade_(2000)" title="Starrcade (2000)">Starrcade</a>, to earn a <a href="/wiki/WWE_Cruiserweight_Championship_(1991%E2%80%932007)" title="WWE Cruiserweight Championship (1991\xe2\x80\x932007)">WCW Cruiserweight Championship</a> match, in which both Moore and Helms grabbed the contract at the same time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> As a result, they later wrestled for the opportunity to wrestle for the championship, which Helms won, although he lost the subsequent championship match to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chavo_Guerrero,_Jr." title="Chavo Guerrero, Jr.">Chavo Guerrero</a> at the <a href="/wiki/WCW_Sin" title="WCW Sin">Sin</a> pay-per-view.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-slam_3-19"><a href="#cite_note-slam-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Moore and Helms would leave WCW briefly in 2001 to wrestle in NWA Wildside, where they held the Wildside Tag Team Championship for one day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-slam_3-20"><a href="#cite_note-slam-3">[3]</a></sup> Helms became the number one contender for the Cruiserweight Championship after winning a match at <a href="/wiki/SuperBrawl#SuperBrawl_Revenge" title="SuperBrawl">SuperBrawl Revenge</a>, but was attacked by Karagias and Moore afterwards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-slam_3-21"><a href="#cite_note-slam-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> Despite the attack, Helms would go on to defeat Guerrero for the WCW Cruiserweight Championship at <a href="/wiki/WCW_Greed" title="WCW Greed">Greed</a> and was the reigning Cruiserweight Champion immediately before WCW was bought out by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Wrestling_Entertainment" title="World Wrestling Entertainment">World Wrestling Federation</a> (WWF).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OWOW_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-OWOW-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-slam_3-22"><a href="#cite_note-slam-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> Helms\' contract with WCW was one of twenty-five that were included in WWF\'s purchase of WCW.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span id="World_Wrestling_Federation_/_Entertainment_(2001_-_2010)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="World_Wrestling_Federation_.2F_Entertainment_.282001_-_2010.29">World Wrestling Federation / Entertainment (2001 - 2010)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gregory_Helms&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: World Wrestling Federation / Entertainment (2001 - 2010)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span id="Early_appearances_(2001\xe2\x80\x932002)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_appearances_.282001.E2.80.932002.29">Early appearances (2001\xe2\x80\x932002)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gregory_Helms&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Early appearances (2001\xe2\x80\x932002)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Helms made his WWF debut on the July 5, 2001 episode of <i><a href="/wiki/WWE_SmackDown" title="WWE SmackDown">SmackDown!</a></i>, using the name "Hollywood" Gregory Helms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-slam_3-23"><a href="#cite_note-slam-3">[3]</a></sup> He was part of the <a href="/wiki/The_Invasion_(professional_wrestling)" title="The Invasion (professional wrestling)">Invasion</a> storyline as a member of <a href="/wiki/The_Alliance_(professional_wrestling)" title="The Alliance (professional wrestling)">The Alliance</a> losing his Cruiserweight Championship in a one-on-one match to another Alliance member, <a href="/wiki/Billy_Kidman" title="Billy Kidman">Billy Kidman</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Helms.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="260" data-file-width="200" height="260" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/26/Helms.jpg" width="200"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Helms.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nHelms at an autograph signing in June 2002</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Helms began wrestling as "The Hurricane" on August 27, and also began wearing a superhero costume. That night, he won the <a href="/wiki/WWE_European_Championship" title="WWE European Championship">WWF European Championship</a> from <a href="/wiki/Matt_Hardy" title="Matt Hardy">Matt Hardy</a> with help from <a href="/wiki/Ivory_(wrestler)" title="Ivory (wrestler)">Ivory</a>, but lost it to <a href="/wiki/John_Layfield" title="John Layfield">Bradshaw</a> on October 22, 2001.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-euro_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-euro-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> In September 2001, Helms formed a tag team with <a href="/wiki/Lance_Storm" title="Lance Storm">Lance Storm</a> who was now managed by Ivory and Helms later picked up a sidekick, in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nora_Greenwald" title="Nora Greenwald">Molly Holly</a> who began to call herself "Mighty Molly", and the two came to the arena in a custom "Hurri-Cycle" (with Molly in the sidecar).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hurricane_7-2"><a href="#cite_note-hurricane-7">[7]</a></sup> The team of Helms and Storm began feuds with teams like The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hardy_Boyz" title="Hardy Boyz">Hardy Boyz</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paul_Wight" title="Paul Wight">Big Show</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Matt_Hyson" title="Matt Hyson">Spike Dudley</a>. Helms and Storm got a shot at the <a href="/wiki/WCW_World_Tag_Team_Championship" title="WCW World Tag Team Championship">WCW Tag Team Championship</a> against The Hardy Boyz at <a href="/wiki/No_Mercy_(2001)" title="No Mercy (2001)">No Mercy</a> in a losing effort.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p>\n<p>During 2002, The Hurricane won the <a href="/wiki/WWE_Hardcore_Championship" title="WWE Hardcore Championship">WWF Hardcore Championship</a> at <a href="/wiki/WrestleMania_X8" title="WrestleMania X8">WrestleMania X8</a>, but Molly <a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_professional_wrestling_terms#Turn" title="Glossary of professional wrestling terms">betrayed</a> him, hitting him in the back of the head with a frying pan, and defeating him for the championship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pwi110_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-pwi110-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> Helms was later <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WWE_Draft" title="WWE Draft">drafted</a> to the SmackDown! brand following the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WWE_Brand_Extension" title="WWE Brand Extension">brand extension</a>, and he won the Cruiserweight Championship from <a href="/wiki/Yoshihiro_Tajiri" title="Yoshihiro Tajiri">Tajiri</a> and Billy Kidman in a <a href="/wiki/Professional_wrestling_match_types#Basic_non-elimination_matches" title="Professional wrestling match types">triple threat match</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cruiser1_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-cruiser1-25">[25]</a></sup> He lost it to Jamie Noble at <a href="/wiki/King_of_the_Ring_(2002)" title="King of the Ring (2002)">King of the Ring</a>. Later in 2002, he was traded to <a href="/wiki/WWE_Raw" title="WWE Raw">Raw</a>, won the <a href="/wiki/World_Tag_Team_Championship_(WWE)" title="World Tag Team Championship (WWE)">World Tag Team Championship</a> with <a href="/wiki/Kane_(wrestler)" title="Kane (wrestler)">Kane</a>, and held them for around a month in an alliance known as Hurri-Kane.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-worldtag-kane_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-worldtag-kane-26">[26]</a></sup></p>\n<h4><span id="Teaming_with_Rosey_(2003\xe2\x80\x932005)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Teaming_with_Rosey_.282003.E2.80.932005.29">Teaming with Rosey (2003\xe2\x80\x932005)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gregory_Helms&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Teaming with Rosey (2003\xe2\x80\x932005)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/The_Hurricane_and_Rosey" title="The Hurricane and Rosey">The Hurricane and Rosey</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_hurricane.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="291" data-file-width="180" height="291" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e2/The_hurricane.jpg" width="180"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_hurricane.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nHelms as "The Hurricane" with the <a href="/wiki/World_Tag_Team_Championship_(WWE)" title="World Tag Team Championship (WWE)">World Tag Team Championship</a></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>In 2003, Hurricane feuded with <a href="/wiki/Dwayne_Johnson" title="Dwayne Johnson">The Rock</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> In backstage segments, The Rock referred to The Hurricane as "The <a href="/wiki/McDonaldland#Characters" title="McDonaldland">Hamburglar</a>" (in part because his mask was similar to the Hamburglar\'s).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> The feud culminated in a match on <i><a href="/wiki/WWE_Raw" title="WWE Raw">Raw</a></i>, in which The Rock dominated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-raw-Mar10-03_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-raw-Mar10-03-29">[29]</a></sup> Hurricane, however, was able to <a href="/wiki/Pin_(professional_wrestling)#Roll-up" title="Pin (professional wrestling)">roll up</a> The Rock from behind after The Rock was distracted by <a href="/wiki/Stone_Cold_Steve_Austin" title="Stone Cold Steve Austin">Stone Cold Steve Austin</a>\'s appearance on the ramp.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-raw-Mar10-03_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-raw-Mar10-03-29">[29]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In late 2003, Hurricane "discovered" <a href="/wiki/Rosey_(wrestler)" title="Rosey (wrestler)">Rosey\'s</a> potential as a superhero and christened him "Rosey, the Super Hero in Training" (the "S.H.I.T."). On May 1, at <a href="/wiki/Backlash_(2005)" title="Backlash (2005)">Backlash</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Hurricane_and_Rosey" title="The Hurricane and Rosey">The Hurricane and Rosey</a> defeated <a href="/wiki/La_R%C3%A9sistance_(professional_wrestling)" title="La R\xc3\xa9sistance (professional wrestling)">La R\xc3\xa9sistance</a> in the finals of a <a href="/wiki/Professional_wrestling_tag_team_match_types#Tag_team_turmoil" title="Professional wrestling tag team match types">Tag Team Turmoil match</a> to win the <a href="/wiki/World_Tag_Team_Championship_(WWE)" title="World Tag Team Championship (WWE)">World Tag Team Championship</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PS131_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-PS131-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-worldtag-Rosey_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-worldtag-Rosey-31">[31]</a></sup> Not long after winning the championship, <a href="/wiki/Stacy_Keibler" title="Stacy Keibler">Stacy Keibler</a> joined Rosey and The Hurricane as their sidekick, "Super Stacy".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> In August 2005, Rosey and The Hurricane lost Keibler as their sidekick when she and <a href="/wiki/Christy_Hemme" title="Christy Hemme">Christy Hemme</a> were traded to the SmackDown! brand.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> On September 5, 2005 Hurricane and Rosey were defeated by <a href="/wiki/Lance_Cade_and_Trevor_Murdoch" title="Lance Cade and Trevor Murdoch">Lance Cade and Trevor Murdoch</a> during Cade and Murdoch\'s debut match on <i>Raw</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> As a result, Cade and Murdoch earned a title match at the <a href="/wiki/Unforgiven_(2005)" title="Unforgiven (2005)">Unforgiven</a> pay-per-view. During the title match, Murdoch delivered an <a href="/wiki/DDT_(professional_wrestling)#Elevated_DDT" title="DDT (professional wrestling)">elevated DDT</a> on The Hurricane to the outside. The DDT caused Hurricane to suffer a <a href="/wiki/Kayfabe" title="Kayfabe">storyline</a> "<a href="/wiki/Stinger_(medicine)" title="Stinger (medicine)">stinger</a>" and allowed Cade and Murdoch to beat the injured Hurricane later in the match to win the World Tag Team Titles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>\n<p>During the next few weeks, the pair began a losing streak, mainly caused by Hurricane\'s on-screen injuries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> During the October 17 episode of <i>Raw</i>, The Hurricane was assaulted by <a href="/wiki/Kurt_Angle" title="Kurt Angle">Kurt Angle</a> at the request of <a href="/wiki/Vince_McMahon" title="Vince McMahon">Vince McMahon</a>. After the beating, footage was shown of The Hurricane ripping off his mask and striking Rosey because he did not help him fend off Angle.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> The next week, The Hurricane <a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_professional_wrestling_terms#No-show" title="Glossary of professional wrestling terms">no-showed</a> a World Tag Team Title match, leaving Rosey to face the champions alone. During the match, The Hurricane (out of costume) appeared at the top of the entrance ramp, reverting to his real name, Gregory Helms, and watched as Rosey was double teamed and defeated. After the match, Helms announced that he was fed up with being funny for the crowd, and that he was sick of carrying Rosey as a tag team partner. This turned him into a <a href="/wiki/Heel_(professional_wrestling)" title="Heel (professional wrestling)">heel</a> in the process.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> On the November 7 episode of <i>Raw</i>, Helms and Rosey faced off in a singles match, which Helms won.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> Subsequently, Helms wrestled mostly on <i>Raw\'</i>s sister show, <i><a href="/wiki/WWE_Heat" title="WWE Heat">Heat</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> On the January 2, 2006 episode of <i>Raw</i> Helms confronted <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Lawler" title="Jerry Lawler">Jerry Lawler</a> over jokes that Lawler had been making at Helms\' expense, and Lawler said that when Helms was The Hurricane, he was entertaining and called Helms a joke. Helms responded by slapping Lawler, who hit Helms back.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> This confrontation led to Lawler defeating Helms in a match at <a href="/wiki/New_Year%27s_Revolution_(2006)" title="New Year\'s Revolution (2006)">New Year\'s Revolution</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pwi119_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-pwi119-42">[42]</a></sup></p>\n<h4><span id="Cruiserweight_Champion_and_injury_(2006\xe2\x80\x932007)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Cruiserweight_Champion_and_injury_.282006.E2.80.932007.29">Cruiserweight Champion and injury (2006\xe2\x80\x932007)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gregory_Helms&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Cruiserweight Champion and injury (2006\xe2\x80\x932007)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>At the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Rumble_(2006)" title="Royal Rumble (2006)">2006 Royal Rumble</a>, Helms participated in an Open Invitational match for the Cruiserweight Championship and won, even though he was a <i>Raw</i> superstar and the championship was defended solely on <i>SmackDown!</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pwi119_42-1"><a href="#cite_note-pwi119-42">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cruiser2_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-cruiser2-43">[43]</a></sup> As a result, he returned to the SmackDown! brand in February 2006 to start a feud with <a href="/wiki/James_Maritato" title="James Maritato">Nunzio</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kid_Kash" title="Kid Kash">Kid Kash</a> and the other cruiserweights. During this time, Helms defeated Nunzio in a one-on-one match.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> The next week, he was supposed to defend against Kid Kash, but Kash was away on a family emergency, so <a href="/wiki/Scotty_2_Hotty" title="Scotty 2 Hotty">Scotty 2 Hotty</a> took his place. Helms defeated him and declared that he was better than all the other cruiserweights. As a result, all the cruiserweights at the show invaded the ring and attacked Helms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> It was later announced by SmackDown! <a href="/wiki/Professional_wrestling_authority_figures#General_Managers_2" title="Professional wrestling authority figures">General Manager</a> <a href="/wiki/Theodore_Long" title="Theodore Long">Theodore Long</a> that at the <a href="/wiki/No_Way_Out_(2006)" title="No Way Out (2006)">No Way Out</a> pay-per-view event, Helms would face all the cruiserweights in a match for the title. Helms was able to retain the championship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> Later, Long mandated that Helms had to defend his title against a cruiserweight each week on <i>SmackDown!</i> to prove that he truly was better than all the cruiserweights. Helm\'s first defense under this new rule was against <a href="/wiki/Psicosis" title="Psicosis">Psicosis</a> of <a href="/wiki/The_Mexicools" title="The Mexicools">The Mexicools</a>; Helms retained by cheating.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pwi119_42-2"><a href="#cite_note-pwi119-42">[42]</a></sup></p>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HelmsCruiserChampion.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="346" data-file-width="251" height="303" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/HelmsCruiserChampion.jpg/220px-HelmsCruiserChampion.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f6/HelmsCruiserChampion.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:HelmsCruiserChampion.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nHelms has the longest reign in <a href="/wiki/WWE_Cruiserweight_Championship_(1991%E2%80%932007)" title="WWE Cruiserweight Championship (1991\xe2\x80\x932007)">WWE Cruiserweight Championship</a> history, holding the championship for 13 consecutive months in 2006 and 2007.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>In early March 2006, Helms suffered a broken nose. After complaining to Long about having to wrestle on the March 10 episode of <i>SmackDown!</i>, Long told Helms that he did not have to defend his title, but put Helms in a champion versus champion match against the <a href="/wiki/WWE_United_States_Championship" title="WWE United States Championship">United States Champion</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chris_Benoit" title="Chris Benoit">Chris Benoit</a>. During the match, Helms attempted to leave, but was blocked by other cruiserweights who threw Helms back into the ring, resulting in Helms losing the match.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> Helms underwent successful surgery on his nose and was expected to miss five to six weeks. During this time SmackDown! announcers stated that Helms had a no-compete clause in his contract allowing him to waive the thirty-day title defense rule due to any injury. Helms returned to the ring on the April 28 episode of <i>SmackDown!</i>, teaming with <a href="/wiki/MNM_(professional_wrestling)" title="MNM (professional wrestling)">MNM</a> to face <a href="/wiki/Super_Crazy" title="Super Crazy">Super Crazy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paul_London_and_Brian_Kendrick" title="Paul London and Brian Kendrick">London and Kendrick</a> in a six-man tag team match.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> Helms continued to defend his belt during pay-per-views,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> but he made more regular appearances on <i>SmackDown!\'</i>s sister show, <i><a href="/wiki/WWE_Velocity" title="WWE Velocity">Velocity</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Helms continued defending his title against other cruiserweights, while on occasion facing off against SmackDown!\'s other title holders in champion versus champion matches. Helms faced <a href="/wiki/World_Heavyweight_Championship_(WWE)" title="World Heavyweight Championship (WWE)">World Heavyweight Champion</a> <a href="/wiki/Rey_Mysterio" title="Rey Mysterio">Rey Mysterio</a> on June 16 and United States Champion <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Lashley" title="Bobby Lashley">Bobby Lashley</a> on July 7 but lost both matches.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> Eventually, Helms became the longest cruiserweight champion in WWE history, as well as the longest reigning champion of any kind in SmackDown! history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wwebio_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-wwebio-6">[6]</a></sup> For much of late 2006, he feuded with Matt Hardy, with whom Helms exchanged several victories in matches on <i>SmackDown!</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> In Helms\' hometown of <a href="/wiki/Raleigh,_North_Carolina" title="Raleigh, North Carolina">Raleigh, North Carolina</a>, at the <a href="/wiki/No_Mercy_(2006)" title="No Mercy (2006)">2006 No Mercy</a> pay-per-view, Hardy beat Helms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pwi122_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-pwi122-56">[56]</a></sup> The two rivals also joined opposing teams at <a href="/wiki/Survivor_Series_(2006)" title="Survivor Series (2006)">Survivor Series</a>, where Helms was in <a href="/wiki/Rated-RKO" title="Rated-RKO">Team Rated-RKO</a>, and Hardy was a member of <a href="/wiki/D-Generation_X" title="D-Generation X">Team DX</a>; Team Rated-RKO lost the match.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pwi122_56-1"><a href="#cite_note-pwi122-56">[56]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Helms went on to feud with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/James_Yun" title="James Yun">Jimmy Wang Yang</a> over the Cruiserweight Title, after a tag team match in which Matt Hardy and Yang defeated Helms and <a href="/wiki/Sylvain_Grenier" title="Sylvain Grenier">Sylvan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> The feud ended after Helms defeated him to retain the title at <a href="/wiki/Armageddon_(2006)" title="Armageddon (2006)">Armageddon</a> in December 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pwi122_56-2"><a href="#cite_note-pwi122-56">[56]</a></sup> In 2007, Helms once again feuded with the entire Cruiserweight division on <i>SmackDown!</i>. During this feud, Helms\' reign as Cruiserweight Champion came to an end at <a href="/wiki/No_Way_Out_(2007)" title="No Way Out (2007)">No Way Out</a>, when he was unable to win a Cruiserweight open invitational, which saw <a href="/wiki/Chavo_Guerrero_Jr." title="Chavo Guerrero Jr.">Chavo Guerrero</a> win the championship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> Shortly after losing the championship, Helms formed a tag team with Guerrero, but they did not win any matches as a team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup></p>\n<p>On May 18, 2007, WWE reported that Helms had broken two <a href="/wiki/Vertebra" title="Vertebra">vertebrae</a> in his neck, one of which was pressing on his spinal cord.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-neck_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-neck-61">[61]</a></sup> He underwent surgery with Dr. <a href="/wiki/Lloyd_Youngblood" title="Lloyd Youngblood">Lloyd Youngblood</a> to repair them approximately a week later. Following the surgery, Helms was announced to be out for a year and a half due to the injury.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-neck_61-1"><a href="#cite_note-neck-61">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-matt_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-matt-62">[62]</a></sup></p>\n<h4><span id="Interviewer_and_The_Hurricane\'s_return_(2008\xe2\x80\x932010)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Interviewer_and_The_Hurricane.27s_return_.282008.E2.80.932010.29">Interviewer and The Hurricane\'s return (2008\xe2\x80\x932010)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gregory_Helms&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Interviewer and The Hurricane\'s return (2008\xe2\x80\x932010)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Helms returned on the September 19, 2008, episode of <i>SmackDown</i> in a non-wrestling role.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> Throughout the show, he appeared in short video promos, called "Hurrapops", referring to himself as "Hurricane Helms", a modified version of his old ring name "The Hurricane", and mocked heel superstars including <a href="/wiki/Shelton_Benjamin" title="Shelton Benjamin">Shelton Benjamin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Curt_Hawkins_and_Zack_Ryder" title="Curt Hawkins and Zack Ryder">Curt Hawkins and Zack Ryder</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> In the following weeks, he mocked several other superstars in the "Hurrapops", ending each promo with the phrase, "I\'m just sayin\'!" On the November 28 episode of <i>SmackDown</i>, a "Hurrapop" appeared in which Helms announced that he would make his return to the ring on the next episode of <i>SmackDown</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> On the December 5 episode of <i>SmackDown</i>, Helms defeated <a href="/wiki/Montel_Vontavious_Porter" title="Montel Vontavious Porter">Montel Vontavious Porter</a> in his ring return.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> Helms was quickly scripted into a feud with the United States Champion <a href="/wiki/Shelton_Benjamin" title="Shelton Benjamin">Shelton Benjamin</a>, defeating him in two non-title matches on <i>SmackDown</i>, although he failed to win a championship match on December 26.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></p>\n<p>On April 15, 2009, Helms was drafted to the ECW brand as part of the <a href="/wiki/2009_WWE_draft#Supplemental_Draft" title="2009 WWE draft">2009 Supplemental Draft</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> Helms made his ECW debut as a backstage interviewer on April 28, 2009, reverting to his Gregory Helms ring name, interviewing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Evan_Bourne" title="Evan Bourne">Evan Bourne</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> He started a storyline where, while he was interviewing someone, a scripted accident would occur, leading to Helms leaving the interview seconds before the person in distress was saved by The Hurricane.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2009-superhero_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-2009-superhero-73">[73]</a></sup> On the August 11, 2009 episode of <i>ECW</i>, Helms was attacked by <a href="/wiki/Paul_Burchill" title="Paul Burchill">Paul Burchill</a> after Helms denied being The Hurricane. The Hurricane later attacked Burchill in the ring dressed in his Hurricane attire, to save <a href="/wiki/Yoshi_Tatsu" title="Yoshi Tatsu">Yoshi Tatsu</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> The next week on ECW, he made his in-ring debut for the brand as The Hurricane, and defeated Burchill.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> He continued to feud with Burchill, who attempted to expose The Hurricane\'s true identity, until the November 17 episode of <i>ECW</i> when The Hurricane defeated Burchill in a <a href="/wiki/Professional_wrestling_match_types#Luchas_de_Apuestas" title="Professional wrestling match types">mask versus career match</a>.</p>\n<p>On February 26, 2010, Helms was released from his WWE contract.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span id="Independent_circuit_(2010\xe2\x80\x932015)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Independent_circuit_.282010.E2.80.932015.29">Independent circuit (2010\xe2\x80\x932015)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gregory_Helms&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Independent circuit (2010\xe2\x80\x932015)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Hurricane_Shane_Helms.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2496" data-file-width="1664" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/The_Hurricane_Shane_Helms.jpg/170px-The_Hurricane_Shane_Helms.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/The_Hurricane_Shane_Helms.jpg/255px-The_Hurricane_Shane_Helms.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/The_Hurricane_Shane_Helms.jpg/340px-The_Hurricane_Shane_Helms.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Hurricane_Shane_Helms.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nHelms posing on the turnbuckle as The Hurricane in January 2012</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Following his WWE release, Helms began wrestling on the <a href="/wiki/Independent_circuit" title="Independent circuit">independent circuit</a>, including for the Canadian Wrestling\'s Elite as Hurricane Helms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> On October 23, 2010, Helms made his debut for <a href="/wiki/Jersey_All_Pro_Wrestling" title="Jersey All Pro Wrestling">Jersey All Pro Wrestling</a>, where he, under his Hurricane gimmick, defeated <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Federico_Palacios" title="Federico Palacios">Azrieal</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> On January 10, 2011, Helms signed a contract with <a href="/wiki/Lucha_Libre_USA" title="Lucha Libre USA">Lucha Libre USA</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> In the promotion, Helms allied himself with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marco_Corleone" title="Marco Corleone">Marco Corleone</a>, and in his debut for the promotion at the January 22 tapings, he defeated Corleone\'s rival and <a href="/wiki/Lucha_Libre_USA#Lucha_Libre_USA_Championship" title="Lucha Libre USA">Lucha Libre USA Champion</a> <a href="/wiki/Lizmark_Jr." title="Lizmark Jr.">Lizmark Jr.</a> via disqualification.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LLUSA_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-LLUSA-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p>\n<p>On January 29, 2011 Helms made his debut for <a href="/wiki/Pro_Wrestling_Guerrilla" title="Pro Wrestling Guerrilla">Pro Wrestling Guerrilla</a> (PWG), during the <a href="/wiki/WrestleReunion#WrestleReunion_5" title="WrestleReunion">WrestleReunion 5</a> weekend, in a match, where he was defeated by <a href="/wiki/Joey_Ryan_(wrestler)" title="Joey Ryan (wrestler)">Joey Ryan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> He also took part in 20-Man Legends Battle Royale, making his second appearance of the night. He eliminated Cruel Connection, but later was thrown out by <a href="/wiki/Shane_Douglas" title="Shane Douglas">Shane Douglas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Terry_Funk" title="Terry Funk">Terry Funk</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In April 2011, Helms wrestled at <a href="/wiki/CWF_Mid-Atlantic" title="CWF Mid-Atlantic">Carolina Wrestling Federation</a> (Mid-Atlantic) where he defeated <a href="/wiki/Ric_Converse" title="Ric Converse">Ric Converse</a> and won the vacant PWI International Heavyweight Championship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PWI-win_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-PWI-win-83">[83]</a></sup> In 2013, Helms returned to the revived OMEGA, now called OMEGA Championship Wrestling, and on October 12, he defeated <a href="/wiki/Shane_Williams" title="Shane Williams">Shane Williams</a> to advance in a tournament for the OMEGA Championship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> On November 16, 2013, Helms was defeated by <a href="/wiki/Chris_Hero" title="Chris Hero">Chris Hero</a> at a Pro Wrestling Syndicate event.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span id="Total_Nonstop_Action_Wrestling_/_Impact_Wrestling_(2015\xe2\x80\x932017)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Total_Nonstop_Action_Wrestling_.2F_Impact_Wrestling_.282015.E2.80.932017.29">Total Nonstop Action Wrestling / Impact Wrestling (2015\xe2\x80\x932017)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gregory_Helms&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Total Nonstop Action Wrestling / Impact Wrestling (2015\xe2\x80\x932017)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/The_Helms_Dynasty" title="The Helms Dynasty">The Helms Dynasty</a></div>\n<p>In March 2015, Helms received a tryout for Total Nonstop Action Wrestling (TNA, now <a href="/wiki/Impact_Wrestling" title="Impact Wrestling">Impact Wrestling</a>) as an <a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_professional_wrestling_terms#Agent" title="Glossary of professional wrestling terms">agent</a> and began working for the company within that capacity that same month.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> At <a href="/wiki/Bound_for_Glory_(2015)" title="Bound for Glory (2015)">Bound for Glory</a>, Helms made his on-screen debut under his full birth name to congratulate the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/TNA_X_Division_Championship" title="TNA X Division Championship">TNA X Division Champion</a> <a href="/wiki/Tigre_Uno" title="Tigre Uno">Tigre Uno</a>.</p>\n<p>On the February 2 episode of <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Impact_Wrestling_(TV_series)" title="Impact Wrestling (TV series)">Impact Wrestling</a></i>, Helms assisted <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trevor_Lee_(wrestler)" title="Trevor Lee (wrestler)">Trevor Lee</a> in defeating Tigre Uno for the X Division Championship, turning <a href="/wiki/Heel_(professional_wrestling)" title="Heel (professional wrestling)">villainous</a> in the process. Helms would then soon bring in <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Everett" title="Andrew Everett">Andrew Everett</a> to officially form <b><a href="/wiki/The_Helms_Dynasty" title="The Helms Dynasty">The Helms Dynasty</a></b>. On the December 15 episode of <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Impact_Wrestling_(TV_series)" title="Impact Wrestling (TV series)">Impact Wrestling</a></i> dubbed "<a href="/wiki/Total_Nonstop_Deletion" title="Total Nonstop Deletion">Total Nonstop Deletion</a>," Helms was thrown into the "Lake of Reincarnation," and emerged as his <a href="/wiki/3_Count" title="3 Count">3 Count</a> alter ego "Sugar" Shane Helms, and after insulting Lee and Everett\'s dance moves, was once again knocked into the lake by his teammates, Helms would later emerge from the lake as the Hurricane, where he would go on to assist <a href="/wiki/Matt_Hardy" title="Matt Hardy">Matt Hardy</a> in defeating Lee and Everett.</p>\n<p>On June 19, Helms announced that he was leaving Impact Wrestling.</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gregory_Helms&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Helms is a <a href="/wiki/Comic_book" title="Comic book">comic book</a> fan, and one of his favorite characters is the <a href="/wiki/Green_Lantern" title="Green Lantern">Green Lantern</a>. He has a tattoo on his biceps which is the Lantern\'s logo and his original WWE character, The Hurricane, was inspired by the Green Lantern.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> In 2008, he got a tattoo of his last name on his upper back. Helms owns a motorcycle called "The Hurri-Cycle", which he got when he was using The Hurricane gimmick. Helms is good friends with <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Hardy" title="Jeff Hardy">Jeff Hardy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Matt_Hardy" title="Matt Hardy">Matt Hardy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shannon_Moore" title="Shannon Moore">Shannon Moore</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> He appears on <i>The Hardy Show</i>, The Hardys\' internet show. He also performed as the <a href="/wiki/Stunt_double" title="Stunt double">stunt double</a> of actor <a href="/wiki/David_Arquette" title="David Arquette">David Arquette</a> in the movie <i><a href="/wiki/Ready_to_Rumble" title="Ready to Rumble">Ready to Rumble</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-slam_3-24"><a href="#cite_note-slam-3">[3]</a></sup></p>\n<p>On March 19, 2007, <i><a href="/wiki/Sports_Illustrated" title="Sports Illustrated">Sports Illustrated</a></i> posted on its website an article in its continuing series investigating a steroid and <a href="/wiki/Growth_hormone_treatment" title="Growth hormone treatment">HGH</a> ring used by a number of professional athletes in several sports. That article mentioned several current and former WWE wrestlers, including Helms who was alleged to have obtained HGH.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HGH-SI_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-HGH-SI-90">[90]</a></sup> WWE has since made a statement on this situation, mentioning that the allegations preceded the Talent Wellness program WWE launched in April 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> On August 30, 2007, an article by <i>Sports Illustrated</i> named Helms and nine other wrestlers to be given growth hormone not in compliance with the WWE Talent Wellness program. He was said to have received <a href="/wiki/Testosterone_(medication)" title="Testosterone (medication)">testosterone</a>, HGH and <a href="/wiki/Nandrolone" title="Nandrolone">nandrolone</a> between November 2003 and February 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup></p>\n<p>On May 6, 2008, Helms was assaulted in a club in <a href="/wiki/Johnston_County,_North_Carolina" title="Johnston County, North Carolina">Johnston County, North Carolina</a>, by an acquaintance, Dustin Narron.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-assault_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-assault-94">[94]</a></sup> An argument between the two of them led to Narron hitting Helms in the face.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-assault2_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-assault2-95">[95]</a></sup> Narron was later charged with assault and battery.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-assault2_95-1"><a href="#cite_note-assault2-95">[95]</a></sup> On January 27, 2010, Helms and fellow WWE wrestler <a href="/wiki/Chris_Jericho" title="Chris Jericho">Chris Jericho</a> were arrested in <a href="/wiki/Fort_Mitchell,_Kentucky" title="Fort Mitchell, Kentucky">Fort Mitchell, Kentucky</a> after leaving a bar. A police report stated that Helms had punched Jericho and the other passengers in the cab they were sharing. Helms and Jericho were given tickets for <a href="/wiki/Public_intoxication" title="Public intoxication">public intoxication</a> and released after each posted a $120 <a href="/wiki/Bail" title="Bail">bail bond</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2010arrest_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-2010arrest-96">[96]</a></sup> On March 13, 2011, Helms was cited for <a href="/wiki/Affray" title="Affray">affray</a> following an altercation at a bar in Smithfield, North Carolina.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup></p>\n<p>On May 5, 2011, Helms and his girlfriend were involved in a motorbike accident in North Carolina, for which Helms was charged with <a href="/wiki/Driving_under_the_influence" title="Driving under the influence">driving under the influence</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jan_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jan-98">[98]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> Helms suffered a broken leg, ankle, jaw and nose during the accident, as well as sustaining other fractures and receiving over 200 stitches, while his girlfriend sustained a broken neck.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> As a result of the accident, Helms\' foot had to be reconstructed with four plates and 22 screws.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jan_98-1"><a href="#cite_note-Jan-98">[98]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In June 2012, Helms\' girlfriend gave birth to his first child, a boy named Sebastian.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jan_98-2"><a href="#cite_note-Jan-98">[98]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Helms is a weekly guest on the podcast "Keepin it 100" on the Jericho network.</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_wrestling">In class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_11"><a href="#ref_11"><b><sup>1</sup></b></a></span> Helms was part of the group called <a
